11/16/23, 21:34 - Temba: 1. Question: What was the Indira Sawhney vs Union of India case about?

Answer: The case revolved around the implementation of recommendations by the Mandal Commission to provide reservations for Other Backward Classes (OBCs) in public employment.

2. Question: Who were the petitioners in the Indira Sawhney case?

Answer: The petitioners included Indira Sawhney and others who challenged the implementation of the Mandal Commission recommendations. They argued that reservations based on caste were unconstitutional.

3. Question: What were the key arguments presented in the case?

Answer: The main arguments involved the constitutionality of providing reservations solely based on caste and whether it violated the principles of equality enshrined in the Indian Constitution.

4. Question: What was the outcome of the Indira Sawhney case?

Answer: The Supreme Court, in its judgment on November 16, 1992, upheld the implementation of reservations for OBCs but capped it at 50%, and it also introduced the concept of the creamy layer to exclude affluent individuals within the reserved categories.

5. Question: How did the judgment impact the reservation policy in India?

Answer: The judgment set the framework for the reservation policy in India, establishing a 50% cap on reservations and introducing the concept of the creamy layer to ensure that the benefits reached the deserving and economically backward sections within the reserved categories.

6. Question: Did the Indira Sawhney case lead to any changes in government policies?

Answer: Yes, the judgment had a significant impact on government policies regarding reservations. It influenced the implementation of reservation policies not only in public employment but also in educational institutions.

7. Question: What is the concept of the "creamy layer" introduced in the judgment?

Answer: The creamy layer refers to the relatively more affluent and educated individuals within the reserved categories who are excluded from the benefits of reservations. This was introduced to ensure that the benefits reach the truly disadvantaged and needy individuals.

8. Question: How did the Indira Sawhney case contribute to the discourse on social justice in India?

Answer: The case played a crucial role in shaping the discourse on social justice by addressing the need for affirmative action to uplift marginalized sections of society while balancing the concerns of merit and equality.

11/18/23, 17:48 - Temba: Ladies and gentlemen,

Today, I'd like to shed light on a significant legal case that has had a profound impact on the rights of minority educational institutions in India - the T. M. A. Pai Foundation vs State of Karnataka.

In this case, the T. M. A. Pai Foundation, a minority educational institution, found itself in a legal battle with the State of Karnataka. The essence of the matter revolved around the autonomy and rights of such institutions to administer their affairs without undue interference.

The case delves into the fundamental question of whether minority educational institutions have the right to manage their own affairs, including admissions, faculty appointments, and day-to-day operations. The judiciary's interpretation and decision in this case have far-reaching implications for preserving the unique character and identity of these institutions.

The judgment in T. M. A. Pai Foundation vs State of Karnataka emphasizes the constitutional protection afforded to minority institutions under Article 30, which guarantees the right of minorities to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice. This recognition underscores the importance of maintaining diversity and pluralism in the education system.

The case, in essence, stands as a beacon for the autonomy and independence of minority educational institutions, allowing them the freedom to pursue their educational objectives in a manner that aligns with their distinctive ethos and values.

In conclusion, T. M. A. Pai Foundation vs State of Karnataka is not just a legal milestone; it is a testament to the broader principles of diversity, inclusivity, and the preservation of minority rights in the realm of education. As we reflect on this case, let us appreciate the delicate balance between regulatory frameworks and the imperative to protect the unique character of these institutions, ensuring a vibrant and diverse educational landscape for generations to come. Thank you.

11/18/23, 19:45 - Kekdaa: Good evening maam, I am going to speak on 
The T M A Pai Foundation vs State of Karnataka case which is a landmark legal decision. 
T M A Pai Foundation challenged certain provisions of the Karnataka Professional Educational Institutions (Regulation of Admission and Determination of Fee) Act, 2002. The Act regulated admissions and fees in private professional colleges, including minority institutions.
The Supreme Court held that minority educational institutions have the autonomy to administer their affairs, including the right to appoint staff and admit students, without government interference. 
The judgment upholds the constitutional rights of minority institutions to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice.
The key aspects of the judgment include:
Autonomy of Minority Institutions: The Supreme Court affirmed the autonomy of minority educational institutions, stating that they have the right to establish and administer their institutions without excessive government interference. This autonomy extends to the selection of students and staff.
Reservation Policies: The judgment addressed the issue of reservations in minority institutions. While recognizing the importance of providing opportunities to the less privileged, the court held that the right of minority institutions to admit students of their choice should be preserved, even if they choose not to implement reservations.
Necessity of Regulation: The court acknowledged the need for a certain degree of regulation to prevent maladministration and ensure that minority institutions fulfill their educational obligations. However, it emphasized that regulations should not infringe upon the essential character and rights of these institutions.
Fee Structure: The court discussed the regulation of fees, stating that it should be reasonable and not result in profiteering. It recognized that the government has the authority to regulate fees to prevent commercialization but emphasized that the fixation of fees should not compromise the autonomy of minority institutions.

11/26/23, 12:10 - Kekdaa: ng new app
use routing
ng g c cart
then other components
4 components needed 
cart,home,recipe1,recipe2
after that add <app-home></app-home> in body of root component

in app routing , give path like 
{component : Recipe1Component,
path:'recipe1'
}
for home 
{component : HomeComponent,
path:''
}
similarly others

then make buttons in app.component.html 
like home,recipe1,recipe2,cart and add router link to it
like <button routerlink>
and add router outlet at end

In every component make header of recipe
then create a drop down of ingredients

ng g s add // service creation
Then in services
make 2 functions below constructor 
getTask and addTask 
addtask(task.value) //pass a parameter
getTask():{
return this.data } //see code for correct syntax

then in whichever component needs service 
go to its component.ts and add costructor(public: _task:Servicename)       //it wll automatically import service

In recipes we ll only need add task
in cart we use  get
make a function in cart.component.ts of delete
//for exact code review source code

Then ng serve

11/29/23, 22:09 - Temba: ### Functions:

1. **Question:** What is the purpose of a function in a database?
   - **Answer:** A function in a database is a reusable piece of code that performs a specific task. It can be used to encapsulate logic, perform calculations, or return a value.

2. **Question:** Explain the difference between a scalar function and a table function.
   - **Answer:** A scalar function returns a single value, while a table function returns a table as its result. Scalar functions are used in expressions, and table functions are used in the FROM clause.

3. **Question:** How do you create a user-defined function in MySQL?
   - **Answer:** 
     ```sql
     CREATE FUNCTION function_name (parameters)
     RETURNS return_type
     BEGIN
       -- Function logic here
     END;
     ```

4. **Question:** Discuss the advantages and disadvantages of using functions in SQL queries.
   - **Answer:** Advantages include code reusability and modularization. Disadvantages may include potential performance overhead and limitations on complex logic.

5. **Question:** Can you use a function in a WHERE clause? If yes, provide an example.
   - **Answer:** Yes, for example:
     ```sql
     SELECT * FROM table_name WHERE function_name(column) = value;
     ```

### Stored Procedures:

1. **Question:** What is a stored procedure, and how does it differ from a function?
   - **Answer:** A stored procedure is a set of SQL statements stored in the database and executed as a single unit. Unlike a function, it may or may not return a value.

2. **Question:** Explain the importance of input and output parameters in stored procedures.
   - **Answer:** Input parameters allow passing values to the procedure, and output parameters allow the procedure to return values. They enhance the flexibility and reusability of stored procedures.

3. **Question:** How do you call a stored procedure in MySQL?
   - **Answer:** 
     ```sql
     CALL procedure_name(parameters);
     ```

4. **Question:** Discuss the role of transactions in stored procedures.
   - **Answer:** Transactions ensure that a series of SQL statements are executed as a single unit, allowing for consistency and integrity. BEGIN, COMMIT, and ROLLBACK are used to manage transactions.

5. **Question:** Can you nest stored procedures within each other?
   - **Answer:** Yes, stored procedures can be nested within each other to create modular and reusable code.

### Exception Handling:

1. **Question:** What is exception handling in the context of database programming?
   - **Answer:** Exception handling is the process of dealing with errors or exceptional situations that may occur during the execution of a program.

2. **Question:** How do you declare and raise custom exceptions in PL/SQL?
   - **Answer:** 
     ```sql
     DECLARE
       custom_exception EXCEPTION;
     BEGIN
       RAISE custom_exception;
     END;
     ```

3. **Question:** Explain the difference between the `RAISE` and `RAISE_APPLICATION_ERROR` statements.
   - **Answer:** `RAISE` is used to raise a named exception, while `RAISE_APPLICATION_ERROR` allows raising a custom exception with a user-defined error code and message.

4. **Question:** Discuss the importance of the `EXCEPTION_INIT` pragma.
   - **Answer:** The `EXCEPTION_INIT` pragma is used to associate an exception name with an Oracle error code, providing more meaningful information when handling errors.

5. **Question:** Can you use exception handling in stored procedures and functions in MySQL?
   - **Answer:** MySQL uses the `DECLARE ... HANDLER` construct for exception handling within stored procedures, but it does not have a direct equivalent in functions.

### Joins:

1. **Question:** Differentiate between INNER JOIN and OUTER JOIN.
   - **Answer:** INNER JOIN returns only matching rows, while OUTER JOIN returns matching rows along with non-matching rows.

2. **Question:** What is a self-join, and in what scenarios is it useful?
   - **Answer:** A self-join occurs when a table is joined with itself. It is useful when dealing with hierarchical data or when comparing rows within the same table.

3. **Question:** Explain the concept of CROSS JOIN.
   - **Answer:** CROSS JOIN produces the Cartesian product of two tables, meaning it combines each row from the first table with every row from the second table.

4. **Question:** How do you optimize join performance in a large database?
   - **Answer:** Optimizing join performance involves using indexes, selecting appropriate join algorithms, and denormalizing data when necessary.

5. **Question:** Discuss the differences between JOIN and UNION.
   - **Answer:** JOIN is used to combine rows from two or more tables based on a related column, while UNION is used to combine the result sets of two or more SELECT statements with similar column structures.

### Subqueries:

1. **Question:** What is a subquery, and how is it different from a join?
   - **Answer:** A subquery is a query nested inside another query. Unlike a join, a subquery is enclosed in parentheses and can return a scalar value or a result set.

2. **Question:** Explain the concept of a correlated subquery.
   - **Answer:** A correlated subquery refers to a subquery that depends on the outer query. The subquery is executed once for each row processed by the outer query.

3. **Question:** When would you use a subquery instead of a JOIN in a query?
   - **Answer:** Use a subquery when you need to compare each row against the result of another query or when the subquery is dependent on the outer query.

4. **Question:** How do you use the EXISTS and NOT EXISTS operators in subqueries?
   - **Answer:** 
     ```sql
     SELECT column_name FROM table_name
     WHERE EXISTS (SELECT * FROM another_table WHERE condition);
     ```

5. **Question:** Can you nest multiple levels of subqueries?
   - **Answer:** Yes, subqueries can be nested within other subqueries to create complex queries. However, it's important to balance readability and performance.

11/30/23, 20:50 - Shivaji W: #include <iostream>
#include <queue>

using namespace std;

class Node {
public:
    int data;
    Node* left;
    Node* right;

    Node(int d) {
        this->data = d;
        this->left = NULL;
        this->right = NULL;
    }
};

void levelOrderTraversal(Node* root) {
    if (root == NULL)
        return;

    queue<Node*> q;
    q.push(root);
    q.push(NULL);

    while (!q.empty()) {
        Node* temp = q.front();
        q.pop();

        if (temp == NULL) {
            cout << endl;
            if (!q.empty()) {
                q.push(NULL);
            }
        } else {
            cout << temp->data << " ";
            if (temp->left) {
                q.push(temp->left);
            }
            if (temp->right) {
                q.push(temp->right);
            }
        }
    }
}

Node* insertIntoBST(Node* root, int d) {
    // base case
    if (root == NULL) {
        root = new Node(d);
        return root;
    }

    if (d > root->data) {
        // right part madhe insert kra
        root->right = insertIntoBST(root->right, d);
    } else {
        root->left = insertIntoBST(root->left, d);
    }
    return root;
}

void takeInput(Node*& root) {
    int data;
    cin >> data;

    while (data != -1) {
        root = insertIntoBST(root, data);
        cin >> data;
    }
}

int main() {
    Node* root = NULL;

    cout << "Enter data to create BST" << endl;
    takeInput(root);

    cout << "Printing the BST" << endl;
    levelOrderTraversal(root);

    return 0;
}

12/19/23, 12:19 - Kapil Spit: What ideas validate the formation of Agile Principles and Values ?
12/19/23, 12:20 - Kapil Spit: Adaptability to Change: Traditional methodologies struggled to accommodate changes in requirements during the development process. Agile values responding to change over following a plan acknowledge the dynamic nature of software development and the importance of being flexible.

Customer Collaboration: Agile emphasizes continuous customer involvement and collaboration throughout the development process. This ensures that the product aligns closely with customer needs and preferences.

Iterative Development: Agile methodologies promote iterative and incremental development, allowing for the frequent delivery of functioning software. This approach helps gather feedback early, making it easier to adapt and refine the product.

Empowerment of Teams: Agile encourages self-organizing, cross-functional teams. This enables better decision-making, faster problem-solving, and a sense of ownership, leading to increased productivity and innovation.

Focus on Quality: Agile principles prioritize delivering a high-quality product by emphasizing continuous testing and integration throughout the development lifecycle.

Continuous Improvement: The Agile mindset fosters a culture of continuous improvement. It encourages teams to regularly reflect on their processes and seek ways to optimize and enhance their performance.

12/19/23, 12:29 - Kapil Spit: In video processing, an unprocessed video undergoes a series of 
transformations to become a processed video that can serve a 
more useful purpose. The image frames from the live video 
recorded serve as the input data and are sent into the application 
via the data source. Once in the pipeline, the data is transported 
via pipes between each component.From the data source, the data 
goes through a series of filters sequentially, each processing the 
data to make it more useful for the next filter order to achieve the 
eventual goal of object detection. Eventually, the processed data, 
which in this case is the input image frame with bounding boxes 
drawn around objects of interest, is served as the application's 
output in the data sink.

1/8/24, 19:54 - Niketan: SinglyLinkedListNode* removeDuplicates(SinglyLinkedListNode* llist) {
    SinglyLinkedListNode* current = llist;

    while (current != nullptr && current->next != nullptr) {
        SinglyLinkedListNode* runner = current;

        while (runner->next != nullptr) {
            if (current->data == runner->next->data) {
                SinglyLinkedListNode* duplicate = runner->next;
                runner->next = runner->next->next;
                delete duplicate;
            } else {
                runner = runner->next;
            }
        }

        current = current->next;
    }

    return llist;
}

1/8/24, 19:57 - Shivaji W: Game of two stacks vala he ye
1/8/24, 19:57 - Shivaji W: #include <bits/stdc++.h>

using namespace std;

string ltrim(const string &);
string rtrim(const string &);
vector<string> split(const string &);

/*
 * Complete the 'twoStacks' function below.
 *
 * The function is expected to return an INTEGER.
 * The function accepts following parameters:
 *  1. INTEGER maxSum
 *  2. INTEGER_ARRAY a
 *  3. INTEGER_ARRAY b
 */

int twoStacks(int maxSum, vector<int> a, vector<int> b) {
    int count = 0, sum = 0;
    int i = 0, j = 0;

    // Iterate through array 'a' until the sum exceeds 'maxSum'
    while (i < a.size() && sum + a[i] <= maxSum) {
        sum += a[i];
        i++;
        count++;
    }

    // Update the count if it's greater than the previous count
    int maxCount = count;

    // Iterate through array 'b' and include elements while keeping the sum within 'maxSum'
    while (j < b.size() && i >= 0) {
        sum += b[j];
        j++;

        // Remove elements from array 'a' until the sum becomes valid
        while (i > 0 && sum > maxSum) {
            i--;
            sum -= a[i];
        }

        // Update the count if it's greater than the previous count
        if (sum <= maxSum)
            maxCount = max(maxCount, i + j);
    }

    return maxCount;
}

int main() {
    ofstream fout(getenv("OUTPUT_PATH"));

    string g_temp;
    getline(cin, g_temp);

    int g = stoi(ltrim(rtrim(g_temp)));

    for (int g_itr = 0; g_itr < g; g_itr++) {
        string first_multiple_input_temp;
        getline(cin, first_multiple_input_temp);

        vector<string> first_multiple_input = split(rtrim(first_multiple_input_temp));

        int n = stoi(first_multiple_input[0]);

        int m = stoi(first_multiple_input[1]);

        int maxSum = stoi(first_multiple_input[2]);

        string a_temp_temp;
        getline(cin, a_temp_temp);

        vector<string> a_temp = split(rtrim(a_temp_temp));

            b[i] = b_item;
        }

    }

}

string ltrim(const string &str) {
    string s(str);

    s.erase(
        s.begin(),
        find_if(s.begin(), s.end(), not1(ptr_fun<int, int>(isspace)))
    );

    return s;
}

string rtrim(const string &str) {
    string s(str);

    s.erase(
        find_if(s.rbegin(), s.rend(), not1(ptr_fun<int, int>(isspace))).base(),
        s.end()
    );

    return s;
}

vector<string> split(const string &str) {
    vector<string> tokens;

    string::size_type start = 0;
    string::size_type end = 0;

    while ((end = str.find(" ", start)) != string::npos) {
        tokens.push_back(str.substr(start, end - start));

        start = end + 1;
    }

    tokens.push_back(str.substr(start));

    return tokens;
}

using namespace std;

string ltrim(const string &);
string rtrim(const string &);
vector<string> split(const string &);

/*
 * Complete the 'twoStacks' function below.
 *
 * The function is expected to return an INTEGER.
 * The function accepts following parameters:
 *  1. INTEGER maxSum
 *  2. INTEGER_ARRAY a
 *  3. INTEGER_ARRAY b
 */

int twoStacks(int maxSum, vector<int> a, vector<int> b) {
    int count = 0, sum = 0;
    int i = 0, j = 0;

    // Iterate through array 'a' until the sum exceeds 'maxSum'
    while (i < a.size() && sum + a[i] <= maxSum) {
        sum += a[i];
        i++;
        count++;
    }

    // Update the count if it's greater than the previous count
    int maxCount = count;

    // Iterate through array 'b' and include elements while keeping the sum within 'maxSum'
    while (j < b.size() && i >= 0) {
        sum += b[j];
        j++;

        // Remove elements from array 'a' until the sum becomes valid
        while (i > 0 && sum > maxSum) {
            i--;
            sum -= a[i];
        }

        // Update the count if it's greater than the previous count
        if (sum <= maxSum)
            maxCount = max(maxCount, i + j);
    }

    return maxCount;
}

int main() {
    ofstream fout(getenv("OUTPUT_PATH"));

    string g_temp;
    getline(cin, g_temp);

    int g = stoi(ltrim(rtrim(g_temp)));

    for (int g_itr = 0; g_itr < g; g_itr++) {
        string first_multiple_input_temp;
        getline(cin, first_multiple_input_temp);

        vector<string> first_multiple_input = split(rtrim(first_multiple_input_temp));

        int n = stoi(first_multiple_input[0]);

        int m = stoi(first_multiple_input[1]);

        int maxSum = stoi(first_multiple_input[2]);

        string a_temp_temp;
        getline(cin, a_temp_temp);

        vector<string> a_temp = split(rtrim(a_temp_temp));

        vector<int> a(n);

        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            int a_item = stoi(a_temp[i]);

            a[i] = a_item;
        }

        string b_temp_temp;

        for (int i = 0; i < m; i++) {

            b[i] = b_item;
        }

    }

}

        s.begin(),

    string::size_type start = 0;

Runtime beats 30 %  means ?
1/12/24, 13:11 - Temba: When someone mentions "Runtime beats 30%" on LeetCode, it indicates that the code's execution time is faster than 30% of the submitted solutions for that particular problem. In competitive programming or coding challenges, achieving a higher percentage is desirable, as it implies better performance compared to a significant portion of other solutions.
1/12/24, 13:12 - Niketan: How much runtime is good solution?
1/12/24, 13:13 - Temba: I havenâ€™t reached that part of wisdom yet
1/12/24, 13:14 - Temba: In LeetCode and similar coding platforms, a lower runtime percentage is generally considered better. For example, if your code has a runtime beats 90%, it means it performs better (faster) than 90% of the submitted solutions for that specific problem. Achieving a higher percentage, ideally close to 100%, indicates a more efficient and optimized solution in terms of execution time. However, the runtime percentage alone may not provide a complete picture of the code's quality, as factors like clarity, readability, and memory usage are also important considerations.

2/18/24, 08:25 - Kekdaa: class Solution {
    public int maxProfit(int[] prices) {
     int buy = prices[0];
     int maxProfit = 0;
     for(int i=1;i<prices.length;i++)
                if(buy>prices[i]){
                  buy = prices[i];
                }else if(prices[i]-buy>maxProfit){
                    maxProfit = prices[i]-buy;
                }
                return maxProfit;
        }
    
}

5/29/24, 09:31 - Sachin Spit: In process automation, data processing algorithms play a crucial role in analyzing, transforming, and managing data to optimize workflows and decision-making. Here are some common types of data processing algorithms used in process automation:

1. **Rule-Based Algorithms**:
   - Use predefined rules to process data and make decisions.
   - Example: If-then-else logic for routing tasks based on specific criteria.

2. **Machine Learning Algorithms**:
   - Use statistical techniques to enable systems to learn from data and improve over time.
   - Examples: 
     - Supervised learning (classification and regression).
     - Unsupervised learning (clustering and association).

3. **Natural Language Processing (NLP) Algorithms**:
   - Enable machines to understand and interpret human language.
   - Example: Text analysis for sentiment analysis, keyword extraction, and language translation.

4. **Optimization Algorithms**:
   - Find the best solution from a set of possible solutions under given constraints.
   - Examples: Linear programming, genetic algorithms, and simulated annealing.

5. **Data Cleaning and Transformation Algorithms**:
   - Prepare data for analysis by removing errors, inconsistencies, and redundancies.
   - Example: ETL (Extract, Transform, Load) processes for data warehousing.

6. **Data Integration Algorithms**:
   - Combine data from different sources into a unified view.
   - Example: Data merging and schema matching.

7. **Statistical Analysis Algorithms**:
   - Apply statistical techniques to analyze data and infer patterns or trends.
   - Example: Descriptive statistics, inferential statistics, and time-series analysis.

8. **Workflow Automation Algorithms**:
   - Automate business processes and tasks based on specific workflows.
   - Example: Robotic Process Automation (RPA) scripts for repetitive tasks.

9. **Decision Tree Algorithms**:
   - Use a tree-like model of decisions and their possible consequences.
   - Example: Decision support systems for complex decision-making processes.

10. **Pattern Recognition Algorithms**:
    - Identify patterns and regularities in data.
    - Example: Image and speech recognition.

These algorithms are often combined and integrated into larger systems to enhance the efficiency, accuracy, and reliability of automated processes.

6/2/24, 23:35 - Shivaji W: from typing import List

def minCostPath(grid: List[List[int]]) -> int:
    n = len(grid)
    m = len(grid[0])
    
    # Initialize the DP table with the same size as the grid
    dp = [[0] * m for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Initialize the top-left cell with the grid's top-left value
    dp[0][0] = grid[0][0]
    
    # Fill the first row (can only come from the left)
    for j in range(1, m):
        dp[0][j] = dp[0][j - 1] + grid[0][j]
    
    # Fill the first column (can only come from above)
    for i in range(1, n):
        dp[i][0] = dp[i - 1][0] + grid[i][0]
    
    # Fill the rest of the dp table
    for i in range(1, n):
        for j in range(1, m):
            dp[i][j] = min(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1]) + grid[i][j]
    
    # The answer is in the bottom-right cell
    return dp[n - 1][m - 1]

# Example usage
n, m = 3, 3
grid = [
    [1, 3, 1],
    [1, 5, 1],
    [4, 2, 1]
]

print(minCostPath(grid))  # Output: 7
6/2/24, 23:37 - Sachin Spit: def minCostPath(grid: List[List[int]]) -> int:
    n = len(grid)
    m = len(grid[0])
    
    # Initialize DP table
    dp = [[0] * m for _ in range(n)]
    dp[0][0] = grid[0][0]
    
    # Fill the first row
    for j in range(1, m):
        dp[0][j] = dp[0][j-1] + grid[0][j]
    
    # Fill the first column
    for i in range(1, n):
        dp[i][0] = dp[i-1][0] + grid[i][0]
    
    # Fill the rest of the DP table
    for i in range(1, n):
        for j in range(1, m):
            dp[i][j] = min(dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1]) + grid[i][j]
    
    return dp[n-1][m-1]

# Example usage:
grid = [
    [1, 3, 1],
    [1, 5, 1],
    [4, 2, 1]
]
print(minCostPath(grid))  # Output: 7
